		'//www.googletagservices.com/tag/js/gpt.js';

		node.parentNode.insertBefore(gads, node);
		})();
	</script>

<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

In this letter, we present a method for sensing the inclination using radio frequency identification (RFID) technology. The method requires standard RFID equipment and assumes that each object is tagged with a passive UHF tag. We use a simple statistical estimator based on the received signal strength (RSS) of the tag reply. The performance is evaluated via experimental measurements, and the results are positive with a good precision within distances of 2 m.</div>

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Radio frequency identification (RFID) technology has been widely deployed in supply chain applications, as it, among others, enables a higher level of automation. Some items handled in such an automatic system might have a <i>This side up</i> marker, meaning that the orientation of the box is important and should be sustained.</p><p>In this letter, we devise an approach to estimate the orientation of an RFID tag based on the polarization of the signal received from the tag. This is a constructive utilization of polarization embracing the polarization mismatch between tag and reader antennas. An example of previous work utilizing polarization is polarization diversity, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>, where colocated antennas with orthogonal polarizations provide a diversity gain as an alternative to spatial diversity. Polarization diversity is also utilized in polarimetric radar systems providing a more complete set of information about the target and environment <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>. Polarization mismatch is, however, often considered a nuisance, e.g. in the area of localization, where a polarization mismatch decreases the precision, especially for methods based on ranging. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a>, methods for estimating the loss due to polarization mismatch are presented in order to improve the precision of the final estimated location.</p><p>In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a>, we investigated the potential of detecting the orientation of a passive RFID tag solely based on its response. The orientation estimate was constructed as a Bayesian estimator, where the likelihood required the mean received signal strength(RSS) to be known <i>a priori</i>. Proper calibration for each different object and environment was therefore necessary. In this letter, we use a simple generalized statistical estimator that effectively removes the requirement for calibration. Since the calibration represents knowledge of the environment, removing it is potentially at the price of precision. However, by using multiple tags per object and estimating their joint orientation, we decrease uncertainty of the estimate.</p><p>The remainder of this letter is structured as follows. In <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec2" class="fulltext-link">Section II</a>, we describe the targeted scenario and present the proposed method to estimate the inclination of an object tagged with passive RFID tags. In <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3" class="fulltext-link">Section III</a>, we present the statistical estimator of the joint inclination. The estimator is evaluated through experimental measurements in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">Section IV</a>, and in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec5" class="fulltext-link">Section V</a> we draw the final conclusions.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>Problem Definition and Proposed Method</h2></div><p>Sensing the inclination based on the RSS of the tag response has been investigated in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_2">[4]</a>, where we assumed a single tag was attached to the object in advance for identification purposes, as illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>. This is a valid assumption, especially for supply chain applications.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6140539/6140539-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6140539/6140539-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>Scenario where it would be valuable to know the inclination of the objects, based on the tag response.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6140539/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>The proposed method was essentially based on decomposing the RSS from the tag into horizontal and vertical dimensions using dual-polarized reader antennas in order to extract the inclination angle from the polarization of the tag response. To achieve good precision, the method required environmental and object-specific calibrations, which in general is undesired. Hence, in this letter we seek to identify a statistical estimator in order to remove the calibration requirement. However, this comes at the price of precision, so to decrease uncertainty of the estimate we propose to use multiple tags per object.</p><p>In this letter, we delimit the number of tags per object to two, tags A and B. To identify the orientation of the object, it is assumed that the relative inclination of these tags with respect to the object is known in advance, and here tags A and B are orthogonal. Their inclinations are respectively denoted <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\theta_{\rm a}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-2-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-4" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-5"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-6"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.48em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-7" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">θ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-8"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-9"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-10" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-2">\theta_{\rm a}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\theta_{\rm b}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-3-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-11" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-12"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-13"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.48em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-14" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">θ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-15"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-16"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-17" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">b</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-3">\theta_{\rm b}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, as illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a>. It should be noted that tags A and B are not required to be orthogonal, but their angular relationship must be known. In order to estimate their joint inclination, we consider an artificial line, C, defined in the plane spanned by the tags. The inclination of C is referred to as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\theta_{\rm c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-4-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-18" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-19"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-20"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.48em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-21" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">θ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-22"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-23"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-24" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-4">\theta_{\rm c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\theta_{\rm a}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-5-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-25" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-26"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-27"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.904em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.48em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-28" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">θ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-29"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-30"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-31" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-5">\theta_{\rm a}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\theta_{\rm b}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-6-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-32" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.48em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-35" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">θ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-36"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-37"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-38" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">b</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-6">\theta_{\rm b}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are in this letter related to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\theta_{\rm c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-7-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-39" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-67"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-68"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.48em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-69" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">θ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-70"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-71"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-72" style="font-size: 70.7%; Basically, the artificial line C could have any inclination, given that the angular relationships toward tags A and B are known.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6140539/6140539-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6140539/6140539-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 2. </b><fig><p>Angular relationship between the two orthogonal tags A and B.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6140539/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6140539/6140539-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6140539/6140539-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 3. </b><fig><p>Vectors illustrating the tag orientations.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6140539/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Simple Estimator</h2></div><p>The RSS of a tag response, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">y</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-11-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-73" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-74"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-75" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">y<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-11">y</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, is obtained in two dimensions using dual-polarized reader antennas and can be written as <disp-formula id="deqn1" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">y_{a}=y_{aH}+j\cdot y_{aV}\quad y_{b}=y_{bH}+j\cdot y_{bV}.\eqno{\hbox{(1)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processed"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-12-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-76" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-77"><span class="mtable" id="MathJax-Span-78" style="min-width: 20.844em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 100%; height: 0px; min-width: 20.844em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: absolute; width: 16.7em; height: 0px; clip: rect(-0.958em 1016.64em 0.483em -999.997em); top: 0.003em; left: 50%; margin-left: -8.345em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1016.64em 4.447em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; The transmitted signal is denoted <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">x,h_{ij}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-20-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-203" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.54em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-208" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">h</span><span style="display: inline-block; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">i</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-212" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">j</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-20">x,h_{ij}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and refers to the channel coefficient, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">z_{ij}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-21-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-213" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; We assume that no information about the signal parameters is available <i>a priori</i>, hence both the channel coefficient and the noise component are assumed to be modeled as two-dimensional Gaussian random variables, i.e., <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">h_{ij}=h_{1,ij}+jh_{2,ij}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-22-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-221" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; Hence, all power variations are caused by the channel model, which is a reasonable assumption for an RFID backscattered signal. We can then rewrite the received signal as <disp-formula id="deqn3" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\eqalignno{r_{ij}=&amp;\,h_{ij}^{\prime}=(h_{1,ij}+z_{1,ij})+j(h_{2,ij}+z_{2,ij})\cr=&amp;\,h_{1,ij}^{\prime}+jh_{2,ij}^{\prime}&amp;\hbox{(3)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processed"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-27-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-348" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-33">\vert r_{ij}\vert^{2}=y_{ij}\sim{1\over\mu_{ij}}\exp\left({-y_{ij}\over\mu_{ij}}\right)\eqno{\hbox{(4)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\vert r_{ij}\vert^{2}=y_{ij}\sim{1\over\mu_{ij}}\exp\left({-y_{ij}\over\mu_{ij}}\right)\eqno{\hbox{(4)}}</span></span></disp-formula> where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu_{ij}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-34-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-605" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; top: -4.381em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-655"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-656"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-657" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.547em 1000.42em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-658"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-659"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-660" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">z<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.003em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-661" style="vertical-align: 0.003em;"><span style="font-family: MathJax_Size1;">)</span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-662" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.183em;">.</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; position: absolute; width: 1.264em; height: 0px; clip: rect(-0.898em 1001.2em 0.423em -999.997em); top: 0.003em; right: 0.003em; margin-right: 0.003em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1001.2em 4.447em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; right: 0.003em;"><span class="mtd" id="mjx-eqn-${\hbox{(5)}}$"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-617"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-618"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-619"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-620"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-621"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-622"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-623"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-624" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(5)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-35">\mu_{ij}=2\sigma^{2}=2\left(\sigma_{h}^{2}+\sigma_{z}^{2}\right).\eqno{\hbox{(5)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\mu_{ij}=2\sigma^{2}=2\left(\sigma_{h}^{2}+\sigma_{z}^{2}\right).\eqno{\hbox{(5)}}</span></span></disp-formula> The mean received power is thus a combination of the mean signal power noise power.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec3a"><h3>A. Estimating the Inclination</h3><p>In order to derive a statistical estimator for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\theta_{\rm c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-36-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-663" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-664"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-665"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.844em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.48em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-666" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">θ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.483em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-667"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-668"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-669" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-36">\theta_{\rm c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-37-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-670" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-671"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-672"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.964em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(2.826em 1000.48em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-673"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-674"><span class="munderover" id="MathJax-Span-675"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.604em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.48em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-676" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">θ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.36em 3.667em -999.997em); top: -4.321em; left: 0.063em;"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-677" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">^</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-678"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-679"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-680" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">c</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-37">\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, we obtain data sets of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">N</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processed" id="MathJax-Element-38-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-681" role="math"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 0.003em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-682"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-683" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">N<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-38">N</script></tex-math></inline-formula> samples of the received signal powers: <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\mmb y}_{\mmb a}=\{y_{a}[0],y_{a}[1],\ldots,y_{a}[N-1]\}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-39-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-39">{\mmb y}_{\mmb a}=\{y_{a}[0],y_{a}[1],\ldots,y_{a}[N-1]\}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\mmb y}_{\mmb b}=\{y_{b}[0],y_{b}[1],\ldots,y_{b}[N-1]\}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-40-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-40">{\mmb y}_{\mmb b}=\{y_{b}[0],y_{b}[1],\ldots,y_{b}[N-1]\}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The ratio between each samples of the <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">V</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-41-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-41">V</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">H</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-42-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-42">H</script></tex-math></inline-formula> components depends on the polarization angle, and hereby the inclination of the tag antenna. We use a simple estimator for estimating the mean received power, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu_{ij}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-43-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-43">\mu_{ij}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, from the tag, and then calculate the tag inclination based on that estimate. The estimated mean power is given by the sample mean over <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">N</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-44-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-44">N</script></tex-math></inline-formula> RSS samples <disp-formula id="deqn6" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mathhat{\mu}_{ij}={1\over N}\sum_{n=0}^{N-1}y_{ij}(n).\eqno{\hbox{(6)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-45-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-45">\mathhat{\mu}_{ij}={1\over N}\sum_{n=0}^{N-1}y_{ij}(n).\eqno{\hbox{(6)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\mathhat{\mu}_{ij}={1\over N}\sum_{n=0}^{N-1}y_{ij}(n).\eqno{\hbox{(6)}}</span></span></disp-formula> The sample mean is the Maximum Likelihood Estimator(MLE) of the parameter <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu_{ij}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-46-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-46">\mu_{ij}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> in <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn4" href="#deqn4" class="fulltext-link">(4)</a>. This estimator is a random variable with mean equal to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu_{ij}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-47-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-47">\mu_{ij}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The variance is given by the Cramer–Rao Lower Bound (CRLB) and has been derived to be <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu_{ij}^{-2}/N</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-48-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-48">\mu_{ij}^{-2}/N</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The estimator of the mean received power is thus an unbiased estimator of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu_{ij}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-49-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-49">\mu_{ij}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, and its variance is inversely proportional to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">N</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-50-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-50">N</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. From <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn5" href="#deqn5" class="fulltext-link">(5)</a>, we know that <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mu_{ij}=2(\sigma_{h}^{2}+\sigma_{z}^{2})</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-51-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-51">\mu_{ij}=2(\sigma_{h}^{2}+\sigma_{z}^{2})</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, hence for small distances between reader and tag, the noise power will be negligible compared to the signal power. For large distances, however, the noise power becomes dominant. The estimated mean power is therefore expected to have the best precision for relatively small distances between reader and tag. The estimated inclination of a tag is then given by <disp-formula id="deqn7" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mathhat{\theta}_{i}=\arctan\left({\mathhat{\mu}_{iV}\over\mathhat{\mu}_{iH}}\right).\eqno{\hbox{(7)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-52-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-52">\mathhat{\theta}_{i}=\arctan\left({\mathhat{\mu}_{iV}\over\mathhat{\mu}_{iH}}\right).\eqno{\hbox{(7)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\mathhat{\theta}_{i}=\arctan\left({\mathhat{\mu}_{iV}\over\mathhat{\mu}_{iH}}\right).\eqno{\hbox{(7)}}</span></span></disp-formula> The joint angle, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\theta_{\rm c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-53-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-53">\theta_{\rm c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, is then estimated by combining <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm a}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-54-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-54">\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm a}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm b}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-55-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-55">\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm b}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> according to their angular relationship know in advance. In this letter, we have defined <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\theta_{\rm c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-56-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-56">\theta_{\rm c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as the inclination centered between tags A and B. Hence, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-57-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-57">\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is given by <disp-formula id="deqn8" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\theta_{\rm c}={\theta_{\rm a}+\theta_{\rm b}\over 2}\quad\Rightarrow\quad\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm c}={\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm a}+\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm b}\over 2}.\eqno{\hbox{(8)}}</span><div class="MathJax_Display MathJax_Processing"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-58-Frame" tabindex="0"></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-58">\theta_{\rm c}={\theta_{\rm a}+\theta_{\rm b}\over 2}\quad\Rightarrow\quad\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm c}={\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm a}+\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm b}\over 2}.\eqno{\hbox{(8)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">\theta_{\rm c}={\theta_{\rm a}+\theta_{\rm b}\over 2}\quad\Rightarrow\quad\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm c}={\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm a}+\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm b}\over 2}.\eqno{\hbox{(8)}}</span></span></disp-formula> In principle, this estimator is scalable to more than two tags, but it is an open question how to map the collected RSS samples and preserve their angular relationship.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3b"><h3>B. Combining Information From Two Tags</h3><p>Signal power is positive per definition, which introduces an ambiguity when estimating the inclination. As an example, consider <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4(a)</a>, where the true inclination of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">y_{a}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-59-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-59">y_{a}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is 20°, and the vector is marked with a solid line and an additional index <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">t</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-60-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-60">t</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The dashed vectors with index <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">f</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-61-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-61">f</script></tex-math></inline-formula> all have the same absolute value as the true vector. However, since the received power is positive, the estimated inclination will be in the interval from 0°–90°, i.e., in the first quadrant, when using <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn7" href="#deqn7" class="fulltext-link">(7)</a>. In <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4(b)</a>, the inclinations of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">y_{a,t}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-62-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-62">y_{a,t}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">y_{b,t}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-63-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-63">y_{b,t}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> are therefore interpreted as that of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">y_{a,f}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-64-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-64">y_{a,f}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">y_{b,f}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-65-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-65">y_{b,f}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, respectively.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6140539/6140539-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6140539/6140539-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 4. </b><fig><p>True signal vectors (solid lines) and the false vectors (dashed lines) all have the same absolute value. All angles are mapped to the first quadrant, which effectively reduces the range of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\theta_{\rm c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-66-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-66">\theta_{\rm c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. (a) Four examples of vectors whose components have equal absolute value. (b) Mapping of angles to the first quadrant.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6140539/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>To maintain the orthogonal relationship between <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">y_{a}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-67-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-67">y_{a}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">y_{b}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-68-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-68">y_{b}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, it is therefore required to map <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">y_{b}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-69-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-69">y_{b}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to the fourth (or second) quadrant. This reduces the range of the estimated <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\theta_{\rm c},\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-70-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-70">\theta_{\rm c},\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\{-45^{\circ};45^{\circ}\}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-71-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-71">\{-45^{\circ};45^{\circ}\}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and will thus give a wrong estimate when the true inclinations of tags A and B are outside the first and fourth quadrant, respectively.</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Results</h2></div><p>In order to evaluate the estimator, we have measured the practical performance in a real-life setup using commercial devices. The experimental measurements were conducted in a lab environment with reflecting surfaces like desks, cabinets, etc., using an Impinj Speedway Revolution reader <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_4">[5]</a> and two Alien Technology “Squiggle” ALN9640 Passive UHF tags <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_4">[6]</a>. Compared to <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_4">[4]</a>, we use only one dual-polarized antenna in this letter, and the tags are mounted orthogonally on a piece of cardboard raised 1.25 m above the ground; see <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6140539/6140539-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6140539/6140539-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 5. </b><fig><p>Utilized experimental setup.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6140539/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>It is desired to investigate the ability to determine the joint inclination within the range of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\theta_{\rm c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-72-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-72">\theta_{\rm c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and as a function of distance between reader and tags. In each measurement, the RSSs from tags A and B are sampled continuously for 12 s using an interrogation power of 27.5 dBm. This gives approximately <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">N=500 </span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-73-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-73">N=500 </script></tex-math></inline-formula> samples of the tag reply in the horizontal and vertical dimension, respectively. By inspecting the measurement data, we found that the variance in the RSS values was in the order of 0.01–0.2 dBm. It is therefore reasonable to assume that similar precision can be achieved using less samples and thereby less time, as the RSS is approximately constant. It should be noted that the CRLB on the mean received power, described in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec3a" class="fulltext-link">Section III-A</a>, is not useful when interpreting the results, as our reference is in degrees, not power. Due to the nonlinear nature of the tangens function, it is not possible to map an error in degrees to a power ratio, or magnitude, of the vertical and horizontal power components.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6140539/6140539-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6140539/6140539-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6. </b><fig><p>(a) Joint angle <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\theta_{\rm c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-74-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-74">\theta_{\rm c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> estimated as the average of the measured inclination of tags A and B, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\mmb x}_{\mmb a}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-75-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-75">{\mmb x}_{\mmb a}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">{\mmb x}_{\mmb b}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-76-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-76">{\mmb x}_{\mmb b}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, respectively. (b) Corresponding mean received power as a function of distance.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6140539/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><div class="section_2" id="sec4a"><h3>A. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-77-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-77">\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as a Function of Distance</h3><p>The tag inclinations are fixed to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\theta_{\rm a}=30^{\circ}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-78-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-78">\theta_{\rm a}=30^{\circ}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\theta_{\rm b}=-60^{\circ}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-79-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-79">\theta_{\rm b}=-60^{\circ}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, giving a <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\theta_{\rm c}=-15^{\circ}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-80-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-80">\theta_{\rm c}=-15^{\circ}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The distance from reader to tag is then changed from 50 to 450 cm in steps of 50 cm, and for each distance, the tag replies are sampled for 12 s. In <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a>, the estimated joint angle, <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-81-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-81">\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, is plotted as a function of distance. The estimated joint angle <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-82-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-82">\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> appears to be fairly constant, albeit 10°–15° below the true angle, up to a distance of 200 cm. At greater distances, we see some significant fluctuations corresponding to the dips in mean power in one or both dimensions. An RSS of −90 dBm is an artificial value specified in the situations where a tag is not read, as some value is required in both dimensions in order to estimate the angle. This occurs when polarization mismatch and multipath fading make the RSS drop below the sensitivity of the reader.</p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4b"><h3>B. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-83-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-83">\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> as a Function of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\theta_{\rm c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-84-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-84">\theta_{\rm c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula></h3><p>With the most consistent estimations in distances within a few meters, we fix the distance to 100 cm and measure the RSSs for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\theta_{\rm c}\in\{-45,-35,-25,\ldots,45\}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-85-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-85">\theta_{\rm c}\in\{-45,-35,-25,\ldots,45\}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. The interrogation power and time is the same as in the previous measurement, and in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7</a> the estimated angles are plotted as a function of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\theta_{\rm c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-86-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-86">\theta_{\rm c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. At this relatively low distance, the estimators are quite robust, albeit the estimated inclinations of the individual tags have errors of up to 25°. However, if we consider the estimated joint angle, we see the expected diversity effect from averaging the inclinations. We thus obtain a precision of the joint inclination within <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\pm 7^{\circ}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-87-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-87">\pm 7^{\circ}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> of the true joint inclination.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6140539/6140539-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6140539/6140539-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p>Estimated joint angle <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-88-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-88">\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the inclinations of tags A and B, as a function of the true <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\theta_{\rm c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-89-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-89">\theta_{\rm c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6140539/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6140539/6140539-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6140539/6140539-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig><p>Setup representing a supply chain application where tagged objects are passing in front of the reader antenna.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6140539/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4c"><h3>C. <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-90-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-90">\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> When Passing the Reader Antenna</h3><p>In the previous experiments, the ability to determine the inclination has been tested in generic scenarios. However, it is desired also to test the method in a setup similar to a supply chain application, and we therefore move the tags on a straight line in front of the dual-polarized reader antenna. This is similar to a tagged object on a conveyor belt passing a reader antenna. The scenario is illustrated in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8</a>, were the reader antenna is positioned 1 m from, and perpendicular to, the line of movement. The additional complexity introduced by moving objects is outside the scope of this work, hence the movement is discretized into steps of 20 cm from −160 cm to 160 cm, where the 0-cm position is right in front of the reader antenna. It should be noted that due to the change in position along the straight line, the observation direction of the reader antenna will not remain perpendicular to the plane spanned by tags A and B. When seen from the reader, the inclination of the tags will therefore appear different from their true inclination. The precision of the estimated joint inclination is therefore expected to be superior in the center of the interval, where the reader antenna is perpendicular to the plane spanned by the tags. In <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a>, the estimated inclinations are plotted as a function of the position with respect to the reader antenna. As expected, we see large estimation errors in both ends of the interval. This is best seen by considering the estimated inclination of the individual tags, where we can see how it approaches the true inclination as the tags approach the 0-cm position. Averaging the two angles, we get a joint inclination with a precision between 2° and 10° in the interval from −10 to 10 cm. At 40 and 80 cm, we see some quite significant fluctuations, and by inspecting the measurement data, it is seen that the fluctuations are caused by sudden dips of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\sim</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-91-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-91">\sim</script></tex-math></inline-formula>6 dB in the horizontal power component of tag A and can be ascribed to reflections from the environment.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6140539/6140539-fig-9-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6170612/6140539/6140539-fig-9-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 9. </b><fig><p>Estimated joint angle <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview">\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm c}</span><span class="MathJax MathJax_Processing" id="MathJax-Element-92-Frame" tabindex="0"></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-92">\mathhat{\theta}_{\rm c}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and the inclinations of tags A and B as a function of position, when passing the reader antenna. The position 0 is defined as being right in front of the antenna.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6140539/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>In this letter, we use a simple statistical estimator of the tag inclination based on the RSS from the tag. This extends our work in <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_5">[4]</a> and effectively removes the requirement for calibration. We enable the use of multiple tags per object in order to increase certainty of the estimated inclination.</p><p>The estimator has been evaluated experimentally, and results show a robust inclination estimate up to a distance of 200 cm and the expected diversity effect when estimating the joint inclination using multiple tags. For tags passing by in front of the reader antenna, we showed how the method had superior performance when the tags were located in the area right in front of the reader antenna, as expected.</p><p>For future work, it would be interesting to see how the estimator performs with tags attached to real-life objects, as the material affects the characteristics of the tag.</p></div>
</div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>
